## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear classical mechanics (oscillatory systems)
**Analysis**: The target variable dv/dt is the acceleration of a non-linear harmonic oscillator, dynamically the second derivative of position x with respect to time t. The restoring force is usually an odd function of displacement x, and explicit time dependence typically arises from external driving or parametric excitation. This firmly places the task in the domain of nonlinear oscillations and classical dynamical systems.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator, c0 < 0)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (stiffening or softening spring)
- Quintic extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonic terms)
- General odd polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * x**7 (symmetric potential expansion)
- Pendulum-type restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (trigonometric nonlinearity, e.g., pendulum if x is angle)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonic driving)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * cos(c2 * t) (periodically modulated stiffness)
- Parametric‑nonlinear hybrid: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x * cos(c3 * t) (driven nonlinear Mathieu type)
- Bistable potential: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 with c0 > 0 and c1 < 0 (double‑well acceleration)
- Pure anharmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x**c1 (fractional power‑law restoring force, e.g., granular media)
- Time‑polynomial driving: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * t**c3 (external ramp or power‑law forcing)
- Exponential nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * x) + c2 * x (Toda‑like potential)
- Combined sine‑polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * x + c3 * x**3 (mixed trigonometric and polynomial)
- Parametric with phase shift: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (driving with phase offset)
- Multi‑frequency forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (quasi‑periodic driving)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Symmetry of potential → acceleration is an odd function of displacement (only odd powers like x, x^3, sin(x))
- Stiffening spring → positive cubic coefficient; softening spring → negative cubic coefficient relative to linear
- External harmonic driving → additive sinusoidal (or cosinusoidal) term in time
- Parametric resonance → product of displacement and a periodic function of time
- Bistable or multi‑well dynamics → cubic term with opposite sign to linear term (e.g., +x − x^3)
- Small‑amplitude limit → sinusoidal nonlinearity sin(x) reduces to linear term x, higher terms appear for larger amplitudes
- Pendulum or rotational analog → trigonometric restoring force sin(x) indicates a periodic potential well
- Time‑dependent forcing → explicit t appears in additive, multiplicative, or inside periodic functions
- Fractional power‑law → exponent c1 not equal to 1 or 3 suggests non‑polynomial restoring force (e.g., granular or contact mechanics)
- Exponential nonlinearity → extremely stiff or divergent potential for large displacements (e.g., Toda lattice)

GT: F0*sin(t) - omega0**c0*(gamma*t + c1)*x - omega0**c2*x**c3 - omega0**c4*x
Candidates evaluated: 50

**Step-by-Step Analysis**

**1. Ground Truth (GT) Decomposition**
- **Given GT symbolic expression:** `F0*sin(t) - omega0**c0*(gamma*t + c1)*x - omega0**c2*x**c3 - omega0**c4*x`
- **Substituted constants:** `c0=2, c1=1, c2=2, c3=3, c4=2, F0≈0.79984, gamma≈0.02484, omega0≈-1.41126`
- **Simplified GT:** `omega0**2 = 1.99164...`
  - `-omega0**2*(gamma*t + 1)*x = -1.99164*x - 0.04946*t*x`
  - `-omega0**2*x**3 = -1.99164*x**3`
  - `-omega0**2*x = -1.99164*x`
  - Combine `x` terms: `-3.98328*x`
- **Final GT structure:** `A*x + B*x**3 + C*t*x + D*sin(t)` with specific non-zero constants.
- **Required basis functions:** `x`, `x**3`, `t*x`, `sin(t)`. No other terms (no constants, no `t` alone, no other powers, no exp/log/abs/cos).
- **Domain:** `x, t ∈ ℝ` (including negatives). Absolute values are forbidden unless zeroed.

**2. Candidate Evaluation Strategy**
- We are allowed to set any candidate constants (`c0, c1,...`) to any real number (including 0) to match GT exactly.
- If a candidate contains all required basis functions and every extra term can be eliminated by setting its coefficient to zero, it is a match.
- `sin(c*t + phase)` can become `sin(t)` by setting `c=1, phase=0`.
- Powers like `x**c` can become `x**3` by setting `c=3`; `t**c*x` can become `t*x` by setting `c=1`.

**3. Checking Candidates**
- **Candidate 1:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*t + c3*t*x + c4*sin(c5*t + c6) + c7/(c8*x + c9)`

  - Set `c2=0`, `c7=0`, `c5=1`, `c6=0` → `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c3*t*x + c4*sin(t)`.
  - Assign `c0, c1, c3, c4` to match GT coefficients. **MATCH.**
- Many other candidates also match because they contain the required core and zeroable extras (e.g., Candidates 2–13, 15, 17–21, 23, 26–47, 49). Examples: Candidate 2 zeroes `c5*exp`, Candidate 31 uses `x**c6*exp(c7*t)` with `c7=0, c6=3` to get `x**3`, Candidate 32 uses `sin(c2*t+c3)*sin(...)` with `c2=0` yielding a pure sine.
- **Candidates that fail** do so because they lack a required term and cannot produce it:
  - Candidate 14: no `t*x` term (only `t*sin(...)`, cannot become `t*x`).
  - Candidate 16: no `t*x` term.
  - Candidate 22: sine term is `sin(c4*x + c5*sin(...) + c8)`; cannot be reduced to pure `sin(t)`.
  - Candidate 24: lacks `t*x`.
  - Candidate 25: lacks `t*x`.
  - Candidate 46: lacks `t*x`.
  - Candidate 48: `t*sin(c7*x+c8)` cannot become `t*x`.
  - Candidate 50: lacks `t*x`.
